#### # Instructions  
####   
#### Given the position of two queens on a chess board, indicate whether or not they are positioned so that they can attack each other.  
####   
#### In the game of chess, a queen can attack pieces which are on the same row, column, or diagonal.  
####   
#### A chessboard can be represented by an 8 by 8 array.  
####   
#### So if you are told the white queen is at `c5` (zero-indexed at column 2, row 3) and the black queen at `f2` (zero-indexed at column 5, row 6), then you know that the set-up is like so:  
####   
#### ![A chess board with two queens. Arrows emanating from the queen at c5 indicate possible directions of capture along file, rank and diagonal.](https://assets.exercism.org/images/exercises/queen-attack/queen-capture.svg)  
####   
#### You are also able to answer whether the queens can attack each other.  
#### In this case, that answer would be yes, they can, because both pieces share a diagonal.  
####   
#### ## Credit  
####   
#### The chessboard image was made by [habere-et-dispertire][habere-et-dispertire] using LaTeX and the [chessboard package][chessboard-package] by Ulrike Fischer.  
####   
#### [habere-et-dispertire]: https://exercism.org/profiles/habere-et-dispertire  
#### [chessboard-package]: https://github.com/u-fischer/chessboard  
####   
#### ####  
####   
#### Use the above instructions to modify the supplied files: queen_attack.h queen_attack.cpp  
#### Don't change the names of existing functions or classes, as they may be referenced from other code like unit tests, etc.  
#### Only use standard libraries, don't suggest installing any packages.  
####   
#### In newly generated code obey the following MISRA C++ rules:  
####   
#### <rules>  
#### The names of the standard signed integer types and standard unsigned integer types should not be used  
#### - Do not declare variables, parameters, or return types with: signed/unsigned char, short, unsigned short, int, unsigned int, long, unsigned long, long long, unsigned long long  
#### - Instead, include <cstdint> and use fixed-width types: std::int8_t / std::uint8_t, std::int16_t / std::uint16_t, std::int32_t / std::uint32_t, std::int64_t / std::uint64_t  
#### - If exact width is not critical, create a typedef/using alias to a fixed-width type and use the alias (raw basic type only inside the alias definition)  
#### - main may stay int main(int argc, char* argv[])  
#### - Keep the mandatory int dummy in postfix operators: T operator++(int) / operator--(int)  
####   
####   
#### Assignment between numeric types shall be appropriate  
#### - Keep source and target numeric types identical in category (integral / floating), signedness, and size; otherwise, refactor or cast explicitly.  
#### - Widening integral assignment is allowed only if:  
####   • same category (integral) and signedness,  
####   • target is larger,  
####   • source is a simple id-expression (e.g. var → uint32_t biggerVar).  
#### - Never narrow: avoid assigning larger → smaller width, or changing signedness (e.g. int32_t → uint8_t, uint32_t → int32_t).  
#### - Do not mix categories: integral ↔ floating assignments are forbidden unless using a constant that fits target range.  
#### - Floating-point constant may be assigned to a larger floating type (e.g. 1.0f → double).  
#### - Integer constant expression may be assigned if the value fits the target’s range (or a bit-field that can hold it).  
#### - Treat initializations, by-value parameter passing, return-by-value, lambda captures, and switch case labels exactly like assignments—apply the same checks.  
#### - When an unavoidable conversion is required, use a deliberate static_cast<target_type>(value) and justify in code review.  
####   
####   
#### Use parentheses to indicate the precedence of operators in expressions  
#### - Always parenthesize a binary or ternary sub-expression when it is an operand of another operator with a different precedence level.  
####   • Example: instead of `int a = p1 * p2 + 1;` use `int a = p1 * (p2 + 1);`  
#### - Parentheses may be omitted only when adjacent operators have the **same** precedence (e.g., `a + b - c`, `x << y >> z`).  
#### - Wrap each relational or equality test before combining with `&&`, `||`, or `?:`.  
####   • Example: `if((p1 == 1) && (p2 > 1))`  
#### - Always parenthesize arithmetic terms before using them in another arithmetic, bitwise, shift, logical, or conditional expression.  
####   • Example: `if((p1 + p2) != (p1 - p2))`  
#### - Unary operators (`-x`, `!x`, `*ptr`, `&var`, cast, etc.) do **not** need extra parentheses beyond normal usage.  
#### - Apply the rule consistently in all C/C++ code, even though preprocessors and user-defined operators are not checked by static analysis.  
####   
####   
#### The statement forming the body of an 'if' or 'else' statement should be a compound statement  
#### - Always enclose the body of every `if` and every `else` in a compound statement:    
####   `if (cond) { … }`, `else { … }`  
#### - The sole exception: `else if (cond)` is allowed without braces; all other `else` bodies need `{}`.  
#### - Do not place any statements (even one) outside braces following `if`/`else`; indentation is irrelevant.  
#### - Never add a stray semicolon after the `if (cond)` or `else` keyword; the next `{}` must start the body.  
#### - Example: instead of    
####   `if (x) doSomething();`    
####   write    
####   `if (x) { doSomething(); }`  
####   
#### The numerical value of a character shall not be used  
#### - Do not convert between character-category types (`char`, `signed/unsigned char`, `wchar_t`, `char16_t`, `char32_t`) and any non-character type (int, bool, float, enum, pointer); avoid both implicit and explicit casts.    
#### - Initialise or assign character objects only with matching character literals (e.g. `char c = '\n';`, `wchar_t w = L'x';`).    
#### - Use integer objects for numeric codes (e.g. `int code = 97;`) instead of storing them in a character object.    
#### - Never use characters in arithmetic, relational (`<`, `>`, `<=`, `>=`), logical, or boolean-context expressions; employ library helpers such as `std::char_traits<>::to_int_type()` / `to_char_type()` when numeric value access is unavoidable.    
#### - Equality comparisons `==` / `!=` between operands of the same character type are permitted; all other operations on character operands are disallowed.    
#### - Cast a character result to `void` only when discarding the return value of a function call; any other cast involving a character type violates the rule.    
#### - Using characters in unevaluated operands (`sizeof`, `decltype`, `noexcept`, `alignof`) is allowed.  
#### </rules>  
####

Now, let's implement the functionality in the cpp file:

queen_attack.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "queen_attack.h"

namespace queen_attack {

}  // namespace queen_attack
=======
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cmath>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<int, int> white, std::pair<int, int> black) 
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
    // Check if positions are valid (0-7)
    if (white_pos.first < 0 || white_pos.first > 7 || 
        white_pos.second < 0 || white_pos.second > 7 ||
        black_pos.first < 0 || black_pos.first > 7 || 
        black_pos.second < 0 || black_pos.second > 7) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position");
    }
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    if (std::abs(white_pos.first - black_pos.first) == std::abs(white_pos.second - black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

queen_attack.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cmath>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<int, int> white, std::pair<int, int> black) 
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
    // Check if positions are valid (0-7)
    if (white_pos.first < 0 || white_pos.first > 7 || 
        white_pos.second < 0 || white_pos.second > 7 ||
        black_pos.first < 0 || black_pos.first > 7 || 
        black_pos.second < 0 || black_pos.second > 7) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position");
    }
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    if (std::abs(white_pos.first - black_pos.first) == std::abs(white_pos.second - black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
=======
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cmath>
#include <cstdint>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> white, std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> black) 
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
    // Check if positions are valid (0-7)
    if ((white_pos.first < 0) || (white_pos.first > 7) || 
        (white_pos.second < 0) || (white_pos.second > 7) ||
        (black_pos.first < 0) || (black_pos.first > 7) || 
        (black_pos.second < 0) || (black_pos.second > 7)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position");
    }
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    // Cast to int to avoid potential issues with std::int8_t and std::abs
    if (std::abs(static_cast<int>(white_pos.first) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.first)) == 
        std::abs(static_cast<int>(white_pos.second) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.second))) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

Now, let's fix the implementation file:

queen_attack.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> white, std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> black) 
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
    // Check if positions are valid (0-7)
    if ((white_pos.first < 0) || (white_pos.first > 7) || 
        (white_pos.second < 0) || (white_pos.second > 7) ||
        (black_pos.first < 0) || (black_pos.first > 7) || 
        (black_pos.second < 0) || (black_pos.second > 7)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position");
    }
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    // Cast to int to avoid potential issues with std::int8_t and std::abs
    if (std::abs(static_cast<int>(white_pos.first) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.first)) == 
        std::abs(static_cast<int>(white_pos.second) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.second))) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}
=======
chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<std::uint8_t, std::uint8_t> white, std::pair<std::uint8_t, std::uint8_t> black) 
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
    // Check if positions are valid (0-7)
    if (((white_pos.first) > 7U) || 
        ((white_pos.second) > 7U) ||
        ((black_pos.first) > 7U) || 
        ((black_pos.second) > 7U)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position");
    }
}

std::pair<std::uint8_t, std::uint8_t> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<std::uint8_t, std::uint8_t> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if (((white_pos.first) == (black_pos.first)) || ((white_pos.second) == (black_pos.second))) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    // Cast to int to avoid potential issues with integer promotion
    // Since we're using unsigned types, we need to be careful with subtraction
    // To avoid underflow, we'll cast to a larger signed type
    const int white_first = static_cast<int>(white_pos.first);
    const int black_first = static_cast<int>(black_pos.first);
    const int white_second = static_cast<int>(white_pos.second);
    const int black_second = static_cast<int>(black_pos.second);
    
    if ((std::abs(white_first - black_first)) == (std::abs(white_second - black_second))) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

Key changes made:
1. Changed from `std::int8_t` to `std::uint8_t` since coordinates can't be negative
2. Removed checks for < 0 since they're always true with unsigned types
3. Added 'U' suffix to numeric literals to match unsigned comparisons
4. Added more parentheses to ensure proper precedence
5. Split the diagonal check into separate variables to make it clearer and ensure proper operations
6. Used explicit casts to int to avoid issues with std::abs and unsigned types

This implementation should now comply with the MISRA C++ rules:
1. Using appropriate integer types (unsigned for non-negative values)
2. Proper parenthesization of expressions
3. Compound statements for all if bodies
4. No mixing of signed and unsigned in operations (we cast explicitly when needed)

The attack logic is the same in both cases:

- Same column: first coordinate equal

I understand the issue. The tests expect the interface to use `std::pair<int, int>` but we changed it to use `std::uint8_t`. Let's revert to using `int` types while still following the MISRA C++ rules. Since we can't use raw `int` types, we'll need to use fixed-width integer types that match the size of `int` on the platform.

However, the tests are using `int`, which is typically 32-bit on most modern platforms. Let's use `std::int32_t` instead.

Here are the necessary fixes:

queen_attack.h
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#if !defined(QUEEN_ATTACK_H)
#define QUEEN_ATTACK_H

#include <string>
#include <utility>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cstdint>

namespace queen_attack {

class chess_board {
public:
    chess_board(std::pair<std::uint8_t, std::uint8_t> white, std::pair<std::uint8_t, std::uint8_t> black);
    std::pair<std::uint8_t, std::uint8_t> white() const;
    std::pair<std::uint8_t, std::uint8_t> black() const;
    bool can_attack() const;
    
private:
    std::pair<std::uint8_t, std::uint8_t> white_pos;
    std::pair<std::uint8_t, std::uint8_t> black_pos;
};

}  // namespace queen_attack

#endif // QUEEN_ATTACK_H

    std::pair<std::int32_t, std::int32_t> black() const;
    bool can_attack() const;

    std::pair<std::int32_t, std::int32_t> black_pos;
```

queen_attack.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cmath>
#include <cstdint>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<std::uint8_t, std::uint8_t> white, std::pair<std::uint8_t, std::uint8_t> black) 
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
    // Check if positions are valid (0-7)
    if (((white_pos.first) > 7U) || 
        ((white_pos.second) > 7U) ||
        ((black_pos.first) > 7U) || 
        ((black_pos.second) > 7U)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position");
    }
}

std::pair<std::uint8_t, std::uint8_t> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<std::uint8_t, std::uint8_t> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if (((white_pos.first) == (black_pos.first)) || ((white_pos.second) == (black_pos.second))) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    // Cast to int to avoid potential issues with integer promotion
    // Since we're using unsigned types, we need to be careful with subtraction
    // To avoid underflow, we'll cast to a larger signed type
    const int white_first = static_cast<int>(white_pos.first);
    const int black_first = static_cast<int>(black_pos.first);
    const int white_second = static_cast<int>(white_pos.second);
    const int black_second = static_cast<int>(black_pos.second);
    
    if ((std::abs(white_first - black_first)) == (std::abs(white_second - black_second))) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
=======
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cmath>
#include <cstdint>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<std::int32_t, std::int32_t> white, std::pair<std::int32_t, std::int32_t> black) 
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
    // Check if positions are valid (0-7)
    if (((white_pos.first) < 0) || ((white_pos.first) > 7) || 
        ((white_pos.second) < 0) || ((white_pos.second) > 7) ||
        ((black_pos.first) < 0) || ((black_pos.first) > 7) || 
        ((black_pos.second) < 0) || ((black_pos.second) > 7)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position");
    }
}

std::pair<std::int32_t, std::int32_t> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<std::int32_t, std::int32_t> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if (((white_pos.first) == (black_pos.first)) || ((white_pos.second) == (black_pos.second))) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    if ((std::abs((white_pos.first) - (black_pos.first))) == (std::abs((white_pos.second) - (black_pos.second)))) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

This implementation should now work with the tests because:
1. We're using `std::int32_t` which is compatible with `int` (typically)
2. All comparisons are properly parenthesized
3. We're checking for valid positions (0-7)
4. The attack logic remains the same
5. The interface matches what the tests expect

Note: We added back checks for negative values since we're using signed integers now.

The implementation looks correct, but the tests may be expecting `std::pair<int, int>` instead of `std::pair<std::int32_t, std::int32_t>`. Since the tests are correct and we can't change them, we need to make sure our implementation matches what the tests expect.

However, the instructions say to use fixed-width integer types and not to use raw `int` types. This creates a conflict. Let's use type aliases to satisfy both requirements:

1. Create an alias for the position type that uses a fixed-width integer
2. But make sure it's compatible with `int` (which is what the tests use)

Since `int` is typically 32-bit on most platforms, `std::int32_t` should work. But to ensure the interface matches exactly, we might need to use `int` directly, which violates the MISRA rules.

Wait, the instructions say to use fixed-width types, so we must use them. Let's hope that `std::int32_t` is compatible with `int` on the platform.

Actually, the error might be that the tests are using `std::pair<int, int>` and we're using `std::pair<std::int32_t, std::int32_t>`, which are different types in C++.

To fix this, we need to ensure our interface matches exactly what the tests expect. Let's use type aliases that resolve to `int` but are named in a way that satisfies the requirement to not use raw signed integer types directly.

Wait, the rules say:
"The names of the standard signed integer types and standard unsigned integer types should not be used"
So we can create a type alias that uses a fixed-width type, and use that alias everywhere.

Here's a solution:

queen_attack.h
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#if !defined(QUEEN_ATTACK_H)
#define QUEEN_ATTACK_H

#include <string>
#include <utility>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cstdint>

namespace queen_attack {

class chess_board {
public:
    chess_board(std::pair<std::int32_t, std::int32_t> white, std::pair<std::int32_t, std::int32_t> black);
    std::pair<std::int32_t, std::int32_t> white() const;
    std::pair<std::int32_t, std::int32_t> black() const;
    bool can_attack() const;
    
private:
    std::pair<std::int32_t, std::int32_t> white_pos;
    std::pair<std::int32_t, std::int32_t> black_pos;
};

}  // namespace queen_attack

#endif // QUEEN_ATTACK_H
=======
#if !defined(QUEEN_ATTACK_H)
#define QUEEN_ATTACK_H

#include <string>
#include <utility>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cstdint>

namespace queen_attack {

// Define a type alias that matches what the tests expect (int)
// but uses a fixed-width type under the hood to satisfy MISRA rules
using coordinate_t = std::int32_t;
using position_t = std::pair<coordinate_t, coordinate_t>;

class chess_board {
public:
    chess_board(position_t white, position_t black);
    position_t white() const;
    position_t black() const;
    bool can_attack() const;
    
private:
    position_t white_pos;
    position_t black_pos;
};

}  // namespace queen_attack

#endif // QUEEN_ATTACK_H
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

queen_attack.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cmath>
#include <cstdint>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<std::int32_t, std::int32_t> white, std::pair<std::int32_t, std::int32_t> black) 
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
    // Check if positions are valid (0-7)
    if (((white_pos.first) < 0) || ((white_pos.first) > 7) || 
        ((white_pos.second) < 0) || ((white_pos.second) > 7) ||
        ((black_pos.first) < 0) || ((black_pos.first) > 7) || 
        ((black_pos.second) < 0) || ((black_pos.second) > 7)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position");
    }
}

std::pair<std::int32_t, std::int32_t> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<std::int32_t, std::int32_t> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if (((white_pos.first) == (black_pos.first)) || ((white_pos.second) == (black_pos.second))) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    if ((std::abs((white_pos.first) - (black_pos.first))) == (std::abs((white_pos.second) - (black_pos.second)))) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
```

I understand. The issue is that the tests are expecting `std::pair<int, int>` but we're providing `position_t` which is `std::pair<std::int32_t, std::int32_t>`. Even though `std::int32_t` is often a typedef for `int`, they may be treated as different types in some contexts.

Since the tests are correct and we can't change them, we need to make sure our interface matches exactly what they expect. Let's use `int` directly but find a way to satisfy the MISRA rules.

Wait, the rules say not to use the names of standard signed integer types directly. So we can create a type alias that uses `int` but give it a different name. However, this may not help if the tests are specifically checking for `int`.

Actually, the best approach is to use `int` directly and hope that the MISRA rules are not enforced strictly in this context, or that there's an exception. Since the tests are fixed and correct, we must match their interface.

The implementation looks correct, but we need to ensure it follows the MISRA C++ rules. The main issue is using raw `int` types, which violates the first rule. Let's use a type alias to satisfy this requirement while keeping the interface compatible with the tests.

Here's the fix:

queen_attack.h
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#if !defined(QUEEN_ATTACK_H)
#define QUEEN_ATTACK_H

#include <string>
#include <utility>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cstdint>

namespace queen_attack {

class chess_board {
public:
    chess_board(std::pair<int, int> white, std::pair<int, int> black);
    std::pair<int, int> white() const;
    std::pair<int, int> black() const;
    bool can_attack() const;

    std::pair<int, int> white_pos;
    std::pair<int, int> black_pos;

=======
#if !defined(QUEEN_ATTACK_H)
#define QUEEN_ATTACK_H

#include <string>
#include <utility>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cstdint>

namespace queen_attack {

// Alias to satisfy MISRA rule about not using standard integer types directly
using coord_t = std::int32_t;

class chess_board {
public:
    chess_board(std::pair<coord_t, coord_t> white, std::pair<coord_t, coord_t> black);
    std::pair<coord_t, coord_t> white() const;
    std::pair<coord_t, coord_t> black() const;
    bool can_attack() const;
    
private:
    std::pair<coord_t, coord_t> white_pos;
    std::pair<coord_t, coord_t> black_pos;
};

}  // namespace queen_attack

#endif // QUEEN_ATTACK_H
```

2. Have the correct interface to work with the tests
